         <h1 class="entry-title" itemprop="headline">
          Gun Owners Buy 14 Million Plus Guns In 2009  More Than 21 of the Worlds Standing Armies
         </h1>
         <div class="entry-meta">
          <span class="posted-on">
           Posted on
           <a href="http://www.ammoland.com/2010/01/gun-owners-buy-14-million-plus-guns-in-2009/" rel="bookmark">

        <div class="entry-content" itemprop="text articleBody">
         <div class="hreview" style="display:none">
          <span class="item">
           <span class="fn entry-title">
            Gun Owners Buy 14 Million Plus Guns In 2009 - More Than 21 of the Worlds Standing Armies
           </span>
          </span>
          Reviewed by
          <span class="reviewer">
           Ammoland
          </span>
          on
          <span class="dtreviewed">

           <span class="value-title" title="2010-01-13">

         <p>
          <strong>
           USA Gun Owners Buy 14 Million Plus Guns In 2009  More Than 21 of the Worlds Standing Armies Combined
          </strong>
          <br/>
          <em>
           That is 14,033,824,000 billion+ rounds of Ammo..you think that is why we have an Ammo shortage?
          </em>
         </p>
         <figure class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_23604" style="width: 395px;">
          <a href="http://ammoland.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/01/nics-background-check-2009.jpg?896bc4">
           <img alt="Total NICS Gun Buyer Background Checks 2009" class="size-large wp-image-23604 " height="200" src="http://ammoland.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/01/nics-background-check-2009-395x200.jpg?896bc4" title="nics-background-check-2009" width="395"/>
          </a>
          <figcaption class="wp-caption-text">
           Total NICS Gun Buyer Background Checks 2009
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <figure class="wp-caption alignleft" id="attachment_22661" style="width: 225px;">
          <img alt="AmmoLand Gun News" class="size-medium wp-image-22661" height="56" src="http://ammoland.com/wp-content/uploads/2009/12/ammoland-logo-225x56.jpg?896bc4" title="ammoland-logo" width="225"/>
          <figcaption class="wp-caption-text">
           AmmoLand Gun News
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Washington, DC 
          </strong>
          -(AmmoLand.com)- Data released by the FBIs National Instant Criminal Background Check System (NICS) for the year reported 14,033,824
          <a href="http://www.fbi.gov/hq/cjisd/nics.htm" onclick="javascript:pageTracker._trackPageview('/outbound/article/www.fbi.gov'); __gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.fbi.gov/hq/cjisd/nics.htm', 'NICS Checks for the year of 2009');" target="_blank" title="AmmoLand">
           NICS Checks for the year of 2009
          </a>
          , a 10 percent increase in gun purchases from the 12,709,023 reported in 2008.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           So far that is roughly 14,000,000+ guns bought last year!
          </strong>
          <br/>
          The total is probably more as many NICS background checks cover the purchase of more than one gun at a time by individuals.
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>
           To put it in perspective that is more guns than the combined active armies of the top 21 countries in the world.
           <em>
            <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_troops" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_troops', 'countries by number of troops');" target="_blank" title="AmmoLand">
             countries by number of troops
            </a>
           </em>
          </p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>
          Of the NICS background checks preformed less than and average .005%
          <a href="http://www.fbi.gov/about-us/cjis/nics" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.fbi.gov/about-us/cjis/nics', 'were denied');" target="_blank" title="AmmoLand">
           were denied
          </a>
          , showing, overwhelmingly, that law abiding American citizens are the ones buying guns and that criminals are getting their guns elsewhere.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           14,033,824,000 billions rounds of Ammo
          </strong>
          <br/>
          Assuming each gun buyer bought 1000 rounds of ammo for each purchase, and you and I know that it is way, way more than that, that would be easily
          <em>
           14,033,824,000+ billions rounds
          </em>
          of ammo fired by USA gun owners.
         </p>
         <p>
          What percent of people were killed or injured by this ammoit is just to infinitesimally small for me to calculate?
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Crime At Record Lows
          </strong>
          <br/>
          This record year in firearms background checks show that Americans are solidly in-favor of exercising their civil right to Keep and Bear Arms.
         </p>
         <p>
          In a year were crime has reached an all time record low what is plainly clear is that more guns equal LESS CRIME!
         </p>
         <p>

            <p>
             It has now been 12 months since gun owners in Australia were forced by new law to surrender 640,381 personal firearms to be destroyed by their own Government, a program costing Australia taxpayers more than $500 million dollars. The first year results are now in:
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              List of 7 items:
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             * Australia-wide, homicides are up 3.2 percent.
             <br/>
             * Australia-wide, assaults are up 8.6 percent.
             <br/>
             * Australia-wide, armed robberies are up 44 percent (yes, 44 percent)!
            </p>
            <p>
             In the state of Victoria alone, homicides with firearms are now up 300 percent. Note that while the law-abiding citizens turned them in, the criminals did not, and criminals still possess their guns!
            </p>
            <p>
             While figures over the previous 25 years showed a steady decrease in armed robbery with firearms, this has changed drastically upward in the past 12 months, since criminals now are guaranteed that their prey is unarmed.
            </p>
            <p>
             There has also been a dramatic increase in break-ins and assaults of the ELDERLY. Australian politicians are at a loss to explain how public safety has decreased, after such monumental effort, and expense was expended in successfully ridding Australian society of guns. The Australian experience and the other historical facts above prove it.
            </p>

            <!-- .comment-metadata -->
           </footer>
           <!-- .comment-meta -->
           <div class="comment-content">
            <p>
             The Spirit of Resistance
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             <p>
              What country can preserve its liberties if its rulers are not warned from time to time that their people preserve the spirit of resistance? Let them take arms. The remedy is to set them right as to facts, pardon and pacify them.  Thomas Jefferson to William Stephens Smith, 1787. ME 6:373, Papers 12:356
             </p>
            </blockquote>
            <blockquote>
             <p>
              Governments, wherein the will of every one has a just influence has its evils, the principal of which is the turbulence to which it is subject. But weigh this against the oppressions of monarchy, and it becomes nothing. Malo periculosam libertatem quam quietam servitutem. [I prefer the tumult of liberty to the quiet of servitude.] Even this evil is productive of good. It prevents the degeneracy of government, and nourishes a general attention to the public affairs.  Thomas Jefferson to James Madison, 1787. ME 6:64
              <br/>
              The spirit of resistance to government is so valuable on certain occasions, that I wish it to be always kept alive. It will often be exercised when wrong, but better so than not to be exercised at all. I like a little rebellion now and then. It is like a storm in the atmosphere.  Thomas Jefferson to Abigail Adams, 1787
             </p>
            </blockquote>
            <blockquote>
             <p>
              I hold it that a little rebellion, now and then, is a good thing, and as necessary in the political world as storms are in the physical. Unsuccessful rebellions, indeed, generally establish the encroachments on the rights of the people, which have produced them. An observation of this truth should render honest republican governors so mild in their punishment of rebellions, as not to discourage them too much. It is medicine necessary for the sound health of government.  Thomas Jefferson to James Madison, 1787. ME 6:65
              <br/>
              God forbid we should ever be twenty years without such a rebellion; what country can preserve its liberties if their rulers are not warned from time to time that their people preserve the spirit of resistance?  Let them take arms.  Thomas Jefferson to William S. Smith regarding the Shays Rebellion, 1787. ME 6:372
             </p>
            </blockquote>
            <blockquote>
             <p>
              The tree of liberty must be refreshed from time to time with the blood of patriots and tyrants. It is its natural manure.   Thomas Jefferson to William Stephens Smith, November 13, 1787. ME 6:373, Papers 12:356
             </p>
            </blockquote>
            <p>
              from
             <a href="http://etext.lib.virginia.edu/jefferson/quotations/jeff0300.htm" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://etext.lib.virginia.edu/jefferson/quotations/jeff0300.htm', 'http://etext.lib.virginia.edu/jefferson/quotations/jeff0300.htm');" rel="nofollow">
              http://etext.lib.virginia.edu/jefferson/quotations/jeff0300.htm
             </a>
            </p>
            <p>
             [A]ll power is inherent in the people  it is their right and duty to be at all times armed,  Thomas Jefferson, in a  letter to John Cartwright, 1824
            </p>

             I dont mind if some of my fellow Americans choose not to own firearms.  This is a free country and that is their right.  What I dont understand, and will never understand, is how those people feel believe they have a right to force ME to comply with their beliefs.
            </p>
            <p>
             Again, I dont wish to make people who hate firearms purchase one.
            </p>
            <p>
             And, criminals break the law.  notice how mass shooting always seem to happen in gun free zones?  Why do you think that is?
            </p>
            <p>
             its because law-abiding people obey, and criminals do not.  There are too many firearms floating around this country for a gun ban to have any positive effect.
            </p>
            <p>
             You statists can go piss up a rope.  Read the post showing how gun control worked in countries with genocidal governments.
            </p>
            <p>
             Its not  happening here and I am glad I live in America.
            </p>
           </div>

           <div class="comment-content">
            <p>
             John Lott, a researcher at the U of Chicago published a report upon researching 3700 counties in the US concerning presence of firearms in the home and crime rates. His unchallenged conclusion was that counties where firearms were kept in the home had dramatically lower crime rates than those counties with some form of gun control restrictions in effect.
             <br/>
             Interviews with convicted felons disclosed that if a robber knew that a home owner might have a firearm, the perp would not try a forced entry.
             <br/>
             Each year the NRA reports that armed home/store owners stop the
             <br/>
             process of a robery/assault over 600,000 times. You have one cop for every 20-25 thousand residents in the US. The Police have no constitutional mandate to protect you. They enforce the law but
             <br/>
             can not prevent crimes. You are obliged to defend yourself.
            </p>

         <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-11701">
          <article class="comment-body" id="div-comment-11701">
           <footer class="comment-meta">
            <div class="comment-author vcard">
             <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/cf34086d653af21cbfb6908292632878?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/cf34086d653af21cbfb6908292632878?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="32"/>
             <b class="fn">

             </b>
             <span class="says">
              says:
             </span>
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-author -->
            <div class="comment-metadata">
             <a href="http://www.ammoland.com/2010/01/gun-owners-buy-14-million-plus-guns-in-2009/#comment-11701">
              <time datetime="2010-03-04T12:15:34+00:00">
               March 4, 2010 at 12:15 PM
              </time>
             </a>
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-metadata -->
           </footer>
           <!-- .comment-meta -->
           <div class="comment-content">
            <p>
             To our dear British cousins who seem fit to call Americans fat and stupid, it appears to me that it is your ignorance or lack of historical memory that drives your opinions.  The memory of the Act of Proscription, enacted on November 1, 1747, in order to subdue the highlands of Scotland is writ large in the American psyche.   We Americans remember, we remember that a disarmed people is a conquered people.  We put our memory down in writing, so we will always remember.  We wrote it down, in every State constitution and in the Federal Constitution, the very simple principle that all free men have the God given right to bear arms.  And yes, we Americans cling to God and our guns  though I, for one, am not bitter.
            </p>
            <p>
             I have read that our Republic was brewed in Scotland, bottled in Ireland and victoriously uncorked in America.  The Scottish Enlightenment is the root of all of our political forms.  If you ever bothered to read the writings of Francis Hutcheson or George Buchannon then it would be ever apparent that America is the fruit of their philosophy which is firmly rooted in the foundation of the Christ.  We are the heirs of the United Irishmen.  We Americans did away with the Established Religion and the Test Act, that oppressed both Catholics and the members of the Kirk alike, think of Emmett, Wolfe Tone and Roddy McCorley.  When our own Revolution seemed lost, stalemate in the North and utter defeat in the South, from the backwoods we Americans gathered. With our own firearms, we met the Kings best at Cowpens, at Kings Mountain, at Guilford and finally at Yorktown.  We remember the words of those who would enslave us, those who called us rednecks, crackers and wild Irish that needed to be cleared from the land.  We remember your ways and your words.  By the possession of firearms we exercise our God given right to defend our liberty, our lives and our property.  You would be wise to remember our ways and our words  No Surrender and No King but Christ.
            </p>
            <p>
             You might try reading the Good Book sometime, in order to come out of the darkness of ignorance and into the light of freedom.  I have measured and weighed your words and find them wanting.
            </p>
           </div>

            <p>
             For all of those trying to argue with the liberal idiots making anti gun comments on this article you are wasting you time. The truth of the matter is this in the words of Ron White You cant fix stupid. Its too bad all of these morons cant be rounded up and moved to their own socialist utopia where they can pay for all of the generous benefits they are want at other peoples expense with no regard to financial responsibility or common sense.
            </p>
            <p>
             Reminds me of a joke I heard a while back about a liberal college student and her conservative father it goes like this
            </p>
            <p>
             A young woman was about to finish her first year of college. Like so many others her age, she considered herself a very liberal Democrat and was very much in favor of redistribution of wealth. She was ashamed that her father was a staunch Republican.
            </p>
            <p>
             Based on the lectures that she had participated in, and the occasional chat with a professor, she felt that her father had for years harbored an evil, selfish desire to keep what he thought should be his.
            </p>
            <p>
             One day she was challenging her father on his opposition to higher taxes and the addition of more government welfare programs. He responded by asking her how she was doing in school. She answered rather haughtily that she had a 4.0 GPA, and that it was tough to maintain, insisting that she was taking a very difficult course load and was constantly studying, with no time to go out and party like other students.
            </p>
            <p>
             She didnt even have time for a boyfriend. Her father listened and then asked, How is your friend Audrey doing? She replied, Audrey is barely getting by. All she takes are easy classes, she never studies, and she barely has a 2.0 GPA. She is so popular on campus and for her college is a blast. Shes always invited to all the parties and lots of times she doesnt even show up for classes because shes too hung over.
            </p>
            <p>
             Her wise father asked his daughter Why dont you go to the Deans office and ask him to deduct a 1.0 off your 4.0 GPA and give it to your friend who only has a 2.0. That way you will both have a 3.0 GPA and certainly that would be a fair and equal distribution of GPA.
            </p>
            <p>
             The daughter was visibly shocked by her fathers suggestion and angrily fired back That wouldnt be fair! I have worked really hard for my grades! Ive invested a lot of time and a lot of hard work! Audrey has done next to nothing toward her degree! She played while I worked my tail off!
            </p>
            <p>
             The father slowly smiled and said gently I agree with your conservative beliefs
            </p>
           </div>

If you were not a felon, and filled out your forms correctly, you were granted a carry license.  Violent crime dropped by 30 %.  36 states now have  this type of law.  Violent crime always goes down afterward, never up.

Cocaine was banned, and I regularly read of 8, 10 and even 12 ton shipments being seized.  Someone forgot to tell the bad guys that they really really REALLY need to obey laws now.

            </p>

             Theres lots to admire about the USA but it wouldnt be top of my list for places to live. On the other hand there are a lot of other places Id want to live even less.

If you dont approve of private ownership of firearms, you have the choices of (a) dont own one, (b) move, or (c) ratify the Constitution.

            </p>

             The citizens -not subjects- of America are regaining their right to own firearms. When the ban on assault rifles was lifted years ago, it was not followed by streets awash in blood as the predicted by the anti-self-defense progressives/leftists. As seen recently in DC, where once the ban on handguns was lifted the murder rate dramatically decreased, the same trend follows gun owners.
            </p>

We ask not your counsels or arms. Crouch down and lick the hands which feed you. May your chains sit lightly upon you, and may posterity forget that ye were our countrymen! Enjoy your friendship with the muslims there who are taking over your country and will change your famous civil law into sharia because you are too scared to stand up for yourself. Crouch down and lick the hands that will soon commit more acts of terrorism in your once-great and once free country.

            <p>
             I agree with rex above that in an idealistic society without any guns in the hands of civilians, criminal or not, the kind of senseless killings committed with guns that we have to singularly live with in the US would not exist.  In reality in the case of this country, however, an implementation of ban-all-guns policy would not get rid overnight of all guns held by gangs, psychopaths, etc. along with normal citizens.  It will take years, decades, or longer to reduce the number of guns to even an approximate zero.  Also it will be a prerequisite to completely outlaw the (huge) firearm industry, both domestic and smuggled, so that the supply itself dwindles to none especially for problematic individuals unwilling to hand over their guns.  I doubt, though, that any of these Wild Wild West clowns who are so brainwashed by the persistent and systematic campaigns of the worlds largest firearms industry operating in the US would welcome giving up their toys in favor of a better society for their grandchildren.
            </p>

             Just want to point out:
            </p>
            <p>
             My right as an American citizen to own a gun has nothing to do with statistics. The truth is that American crime rates are lower than our counterparts in Europe (
             <a href="http://www.renewamerica.com/columns/kouri/060220" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.renewamerica.com/columns/kouri/060220', 'http://www.renewamerica.com/columns/kouri/060220');" rel="nofollow">
              http://www.renewamerica.com/columns/kouri/060220
             </a>
             ), so those liberals who seek to pursue that straw man will find the ground ripped out from under their feet swiftly enough.
            </p>
            <p>
             But the real argument and point is this: I am a free man, the descendant of Saxons, Picts, the Cherokee, and Romans.
            </p>
            <p>
             I am not some serf to be disarmed at my lords whim. I am not a peasant to be slaughtered by mlords enemies when he is off to war. (In this case, when the police are over-stretched in my high-crime area and cant respond to my needs in time, something that has occurred twice now.)
            </p>
            <p>
             In fact, I have no lord. I am an American freeman, not some knee-bending European who grovels at the feet of the modern monarchs of socialism.
            </p>
            <p>
             And my firearms, not the honeyed promises of fork-tongued politicians, are what make me different from my European counterpart.
            </p>
            <p>
             This year will go down in history. For the first time, a civilized nation has full gun registration. Our streets will be safer, our police more efficient, and the world will follow our lead into the future!
             <br/>
             -Adolph Hitler
            </p>

         <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-46632">
          <article class="comment-body" id="div-comment-46632">
           <footer class="comment-meta">
            <div class="comment-author vcard">
             <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0a7e1523c08259859e31bcdf0e11e190?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0a7e1523c08259859e31bcdf0e11e190?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="32"/>
             <b class="fn">
              canemah
             </b>
             <span class="says">
              says:
             </span>
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-author -->
            <div class="comment-metadata">
             <a href="http://www.ammoland.com/2010/01/gun-owners-buy-14-million-plus-guns-in-2009/#comment-46632">
              <time datetime="2011-06-08T21:52:07+00:00">
               June 8, 2011 at 9:52 PM
              </time>
             </a>
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-metadata -->
           </footer>
           <!-- .comment-meta -->
           <div class="comment-content">
            <p>
             The Gun Is Civilization by Maj. L. Caudill USMC (Ret)
            </p>
            <p>
             Human beings only have two ways to deal with one another: reason and force. If you want me to do something for you, you have a choice of either convincing me via argument, or force me to do your bidding under threat of force. Every human interaction falls into one of those two categories, without exception.
            </p>
            <p>
             Reason or force, thats it.
            </p>
            <p>
             In a truly moral and civilized society, people exclusively interact through persuasion. Force has no place as a valid method of social interaction, and the only thing that removes force from the menu is the personal firearm, as paradoxical as it may sound to some.
            </p>
            <p>
             When I carry a gun, you cannot deal with me by force. You have to use reason and try to persuade me, because I have a way to negate your threat or employment of force.
            </p>
            <p>
             The gun is the only personal weapon that puts a 100-pound woman on equal footing with a 220-pound mugger, a 75-year old retiree on equal footing with a 19-year old gang banger, and a single guy on equal footing with a carload of drunk guys with baseball bats. The gun removes the disparity in physical strength, size, or numbers between a potential attacker and a defender.
            </p>
            <p>
             There are plenty of people who consider the gun as the source of bad force equations. These are the people who think that wed be more civilized if all guns were removed from society, because a firearm makes it easier for a [armed] mugger to do his job. That, of course, is only true if the muggers potential victims are mostly disarmed either by choice or by legislative fiatit has no validity when most of a muggers potential marks are armed.
            </p>
            <p>
             People who argue for the banning of arms ask for automatic rule by the young, the strong, and the many, and thats the exact opposite of a civilized society. A mugger, even an armed one, can only make a successful living in a society where the state has granted him a force monopoly.
            </p>
            <p>
             Then theres the argument that the gun makes confrontations lethal that otherwise would only result in injury. This argument is fallacious in several ways. Without guns involved, confrontations are won by the physically superior party inflicting overwhelming injury on the loser.
            </p>
            <p>
             People who think that fists, bats, sticks, or stones dont constitute lethal force watch too much TV, where people take beatings and come out of it with a bloody lip at worst. The fact that the gun makes lethal force easier works solely in favor of the weaker defender, not the stronger attacker. If both are armed, the field is level.
            </p>
            <p>
             The gun is the only weapon thats as lethal in the hands of an octogenarian as it is in the hands of a weight lifter. It simply wouldnt work as well as a force equalizer if it wasnt both lethal and easily employable.
            </p>
            <p>
             When I carry a gun, I dont do so because I am looking for a fight, but because Im looking to be left alone. The gun at my side means that I cannot be forced, only persuaded. I dont carry it because Im afraid, but because it enables me to be unafraid. It doesnt limit the actions of those who would interact with me through reason, only the actions of those who would do so by force. It removes force from the equation and thats why carrying a gun is a civilized act
            </p>
           </div>
           <!-- .comment-content -->

            <!-- .comment-author -->
            <div class="comment-metadata">
             <a href="http://www.ammoland.com/2010/01/gun-owners-buy-14-million-plus-guns-in-2009/#comment-52227">
              <time datetime="2011-10-26T03:27:44+00:00">
               October 26, 2011 at 3:27 AM
              </time>
             </a>
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-metadata -->
           </footer>
           <!-- .comment-meta -->
           <div class="comment-content">
            <p>
             Eastwood said on January 30th, 2010 at 7:29 PM:
            </p>
            <p>
             There is no correlation (sorry, link) between high gun sales and lowering crime rates. Thats just two unconnected statistics.
            </p>
            <p>
             There IS a correlation (sorry again, link) between the violence of US society and its high gun sales.
            </p>
            <p>
             You are confusing two concepts. There is a positive correlation between high gun sales and lower crime rates and a negative correlation between the violence of US society and gun sales. Corelation does not guarantee causation so we cannot affirm fron this correlation that more guns mean lower crime rates (there are other ways to prove this point) but it is very difficult to substain that higher gun sales produce higher crime rates since the correlation between this two variables is negative.
            </p>
           </div>

The crimes perpetrated by people like the bank executives who made all the toxic loans which caused the financial crash, the employers like Wallmart who pay wages so low, the taxpayer has to supplement their pay. Buy all the guns you want, you wont stop the big-time criminals who buy your politicians.
            </p>
           </div>
